    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer5731360878897759732"><i>Librarian's Note: Alternate-cover edition for ISBN <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44777238-a-time-to-kill' rel='nofollow noopener'>0385338600 / 9780385338608</a></i><br/><br/>Before "The Firm" and "The Pelican Brief" made him a superstar, John Grisham wrote this riveting story of retribution and justice. In this searing courtroom drama, best-selling author John Grisham probes the savage depths of racial violence, as he delivers a compelling tale of uncertain justice in</span>
  <span id="freeText5731360878897759732" style="display:none"><i>Librarian's Note: Alternate-cover edition for ISBN <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44777238-a-time-to-kill" rel="nofollow noopener">0385338600 / 9780385338608</a></i><br /><br />Before "The Firm" and "The Pelican Brief" made him a superstar, John Grisham wrote this riveting story of retribution and justice. In this searing courtroom drama, best-selling author John Grisham probes the savage depths of racial violence, as he delivers a compelling tale of uncertain justice in a small southern town, Clanton, Mississippi. <br /><br />The life of a ten-year-old girl is shattered by two drunken and remorseless young men. The mostly white town reacts with shock and horror at the inhuman crime. Until her black father acquires an assault rifle and takes matters into his hands.<br /><br />For ten days, as burning crosses and the crack of sniper fire spread through the streets of Clanton, the nation sits spellbound as young defense attorney Jake Brigance struggles to save his client's life, and then his own.</span>

      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_957').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_134617624" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134617624" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134617624?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=1980-1989">1980-1989</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=legal">legal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=popcorn">popcorn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134617624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13743977183806491076"><b>Considered</b> Grisham's <b>best novel</b> by many readers far more <b>perspicacious</b> than <b>moi</b>, this well-written, <b>emotionally-charged</b> thriller certainly delivers. While it doesn't <b>rank</b> as my <b>eye's</b> own personal <b>apple</b>, I can certainly see why it is esteemed by fans of both the legal-thriller and Grisham. <br/><br/>Despite being fast-paced and a true page-turner (what I would call a <b>popcorn-read</b>), there's a gravity and social conscience that pervades the story and adds a weight to the narrative. There is depth here, more </span>
  <span id="freeText13743977183806491076" style="display:none"><b>Considered</b> Grisham's <b>best novel</b> by many readers far more <b>perspicacious</b> than <b>moi</b>, this well-written, <b>emotionally-charged</b> thriller certainly delivers. While it doesn't <b>rank</b> as my <b>eye's</b> own personal <b>apple</b>, I can certainly see why it is esteemed by fans of both the legal-thriller and Grisham. <br><br>Despite being fast-paced and a true page-turner (what I would call a <b>popcorn-read</b>), there's a gravity and social conscience that pervades the story and adds a weight to the narrative. There is depth here, more than I expected. <br><br>Setting aside for the moment my gripes over some of the language used in the book (one vulgarity in particular), Grisham does a nice job of capturing the setting and providing an authentic feel and voice to his characters. Overall, a satisfying read that held my attention throughout. <br><br><b><u>PLOT SUMMARY</u>:</b><br><br>Despite its brisky pace, Grisham’s Mississippi-based legal thriller deals with some tough, serious issues (e.g., race-relations, vigilantism and “justice versus lawful”). The plot centers on the trial of a poor black father who murders the two white shit stains who raped, tortured and brutalized his 10 year-old daughter. The crime and the subsequent trial triggers a firestorm of racial tension as factions on both sides become vocal and volatile. <br><br>From the opening pages that describe the brutal rape (which was gut-wrenching in the extreme to experience, especially as a dad) through the final reading of the verdict, Grisham drives the narrative effortlessly and keeps the reader hooked and engaged. His story-telling is excellent. <br> <br><b><u>THOUGHTS</u>:</b><br><br><b>However...</b><br>...now that I have both seen the movie version and read the book, my final verdict is that the film is both more enjoyable and the higher quality product of the two. I say this <b>despite</b> the fact that the movie is arguably the <b>“sweatiest”</b> most <b>lathery</b> film in American history and my wife and I crack up about that every time we see it. <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Hollywood%20moviess/?action=view&amp;current=timetokill-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342428i/698160.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Hollywood%20moviess/?action=view&amp;current=entertainment_sweat_movs_time_kill-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342428i/698161.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Those pictures don’t do credit to the muggy, <b>perspiration-overload</b> of the real thing, but if you haven’t seen it, trust me…the movie dripped <b>sudor</b> from every pore like a hooker in church. Words like sheen and glistening are too understated. It was more like the actors showered, got dressed without drying off, walked through a “mister” and then wiped down with a moist towelette before every...single...scene.<br> <br>Now, not everyone was complaining about the <b>drenchiness</b> since it was Matthew McConaughey, Sam “it’s the one that says Bad MF” Jackson, Ashley Judd and Sandra Bullock doing the sweating, but still...hilarious and a bit distracting. <br><br><b><u>BOOK GRIPES</u>:</b><br><br>Keep in mind that I liked the book, so my gripes below really point towards why I didn't rate the book higher than 3 stars.<br><br><b>1.</b> <u>Too much fluff</u>: When you can take a 528 page book and condense it into a 2+ hour movie that captures perfectly the essence of the story and manages to be even more emotionally powerful, it indicates that the novel was a little thin in the story department. This is the case here. While the expanded story and segues are interesting, the central plot contained too much <b>unnecessariness</b> that could’ve been easily discarded without touching the heart of the story...as the filmmakers did. <br><br><b>2.</b> <u>Excessive use of "N" word</u>: Given that the novel is set in 1984, I had a real problem with the significant use of the “N” word* in the story. <br>*(<i>No, <b>South Park</b> fans, I am not referring to “nagger.”</i>). <br><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Cartoon%20TV/?action=view&amp;current=SPWATJJ1-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342428i/698162.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br>Had this been set in the 50’s or 60’s, I would have seen it as a product of the times and swallowed my uncomfortableness. However, it just seems odd that as late as 1984, the word (and the frame of mind that goes with it) would be used so casually and regularly. Given that Grisham is from the South and went to school in Mississippi, he may be spot on with his characterization, and he probably is. If true, this is just very, very sad. Still, its constant use grated on me and I thought the movie did a much better job with the dialogue. This is coming from someone who does not normally favor filtering words through the PC processor. <br><br><b>3.</b> <u>The Main Character</u>: Jake Brigance is not nearly as likeable in the book as he in the movie and I found it hard to engage with him. Now I think we can all agree that Matt McConaughey is not exactly a high level thespian. <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Cartoon%20TV/?action=view&amp;current=medium_43a09602c074755a733433ad21fe698c-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342428i/698163.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>However, he did bring the right tone to this role and I found myself comparing the novel’s version unfavorably. <br><br><b>4.</b> <u>The Ending</u>: Again, I liked the movie version so, so, so much better. While the main outcome is the same, I really liked the way the movie handled the climactic closing argument and was disappointed in the novels path to the verdict. I also really enjoyed the last scene in the movie where Jake and his family go to a barbeque at Carl Lee’s house where their two daughters can play. I thought it was perfect. <br><br>Okay, so enough griping. I thought the book was good. I thought the movie was very good. If you've seen the movie, I don't think you are missing much by skipping the book. However, if you haven't seen the film, I would recommend reading the book first and then watching the adaptation. I think you will enjoy both.<br><br>3.0 stars. Recommended. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13743977183806491076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7698460269826447844">A Time to Kill, John Grisham<br/><br/>A Time to Kill is a 1988 legal thriller by John Grisham. It was Grisham's first novel. <br/>In the small town of Clanton, in fictional Ford County, Mississippi, a ten-year-old African-American girl named Tonya Hailey is viciously raped and beaten by two white supremacists, James "Pete" Willard and Billy Ray Cobb. <br/><br/>Tonya is later found and rushed to the hospital while Pete and Billy Ray are heard bragging at a roadside bar about their crime. Tonya's distraught and outraged f</span>
  <span id="freeText7698460269826447844" style="display:none">A Time to Kill, John Grisham<br /><br />A Time to Kill is a 1988 legal thriller by John Grisham. It was Grisham's first novel. <br />In the small town of Clanton, in fictional Ford County, Mississippi, a ten-year-old African-American girl named Tonya Hailey is viciously raped and beaten by two white supremacists, James "Pete" Willard and Billy Ray Cobb. <br /><br />Tonya is later found and rushed to the hospital while Pete and Billy Ray are heard bragging at a roadside bar about their crime. Tonya's distraught and outraged father, Carl Lee Hailey, consults his friend Jake Brigance, a white attorney who had previously represented Hailey's brother, on whether he could get himself acquitted if he killed the two men. <br /><br />Jake tells Carl Lee not to do anything stupid, but admits that if it had been his daughter, he would kill the rapists. Carl Lee is determined to avenge Tonya and, while Pete and Billy Ray are being led into holding after their bond hearing, he kills both men with an M16 rifle.<br /><br />Carl Lee is charged with capital murder. Despite efforts to persuade Carl Lee to retain high-powered attorneys, he elects to be represented by Jake. Helping Jake are two loyal friends, disbarred attorney Lucien Wilbanks and sleazy divorce lawyer Harry Rex Vonner. <br /><br />Later, the team is assisted by liberal law student Ellen Roark, who has prior experience with death penalty cases and offers her services as a temporary clerk pro bono. Ellen appears to be interested in Jake romantically, but the married Jake resists her overtures. <br /><br />The team also receives some illicit behind-the-scenes help from black county sheriff Ozzie Walls, a figure beloved by the black community and also well respected by the white community who upholds the law by arresting Carl Lee but, as the father of two daughters of his own, privately supports Carl Lee and gives him special treatment while in jail and goes out of the way to assist Jake in any way he legally can. <br /><br />Carl Lee is prosecuted by Ford County's corrupt district attorney, Rufus Buckley, who hopes that the case will boost his political career. It is claimed that the judge presiding over Carl Lee's trial, Omar "Ichabod" Noose, has been intimidated by local white supremacist elements. This proves true when, despite having no history of racist inclinations in his rulings, Noose refuses Jake's perfectly reasonable request for a change of venue, even though the racial make-up of Ford County virtually guarantees an all-white jury.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه اکتبر سال 2001 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: زمانی برای کشتن؛ نویسنده: جان گریشام؛ مترجم هادی عادلپور؛ مشخصات نشر تهران، کوشش، 1378، در 526ص؛ شابک 9646636145؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: زمانی برای کشتن؛ نویسنده جان گریشام؛ مترجم جواد سید اشرف؛ مشخصات نشر تهران، زرین، 1378، در 640ص؛ شابک 9644070178؛ <br /><br />داستان وکیل جوانی به نام «جیک بریگانس» است، که دفاع از یک متهم سیاهپوست، در برابر هیئت منصفه ای سفیدپوست را، بر دوش میگیرد، جریان بسیار پیچیده، اما جذاب و شیرین پیش میرود؛ البته از نظر کسی که به سیستم قضایی آمریکا علاقه هم داشته باشد؛ «زمانی برای کشتن»، نخستین کتاب «جان گریشام»، و گویا نزدیکترین اثر، به شخصیت ایشان باشد؛ «تونیا»، دختر دهساله ی «کارلی هیلی»، کارگر سیاهپوست شهر «فورت کانتی»، برای خرید از خانه خارج می‌شود، ولی دیگر باز نمی‌گردد؛ پس از جستجو، تنها سبد خرید دخترک پیدا می‌شود، و اثری از او نیست، تا اینکه «کارل هیلی»، از «اوزی والز»، کلانتر شهر، یاری می‌خواهد؛ کلانتر نیروهای خود را برای یافتن دخترک به کار می‌گیرد، ولی موفق نمی‌شوند او را بیابند؛ ماهیگیران دخترک را در حالیکه دست و پایش طناب پیچ شده و به شدت مورد آزار و اذیت قرار گرفته، پیدا می‌کنند؛ «تونیا»ی مجروح از دو جوان سفیدپوست و وانتی زردرنگ حرف میزند و...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_2548946471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2548946471" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17042835-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486434279p2/17042835.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2548946471?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/17042835-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548946471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8152204186133153759">This 1988 first Grisham novel is outstanding. 10 of 10 stars!</span>

          </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099201212" href="/book/show/907830.A_Time_To_Kill">review of another edition</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9351872825130020295">Original Mid-90s Star Only Review – 5 Stars<br/>Re-Read in 2020 Review – 4 Stars<br/><br/>You will notice a drop in the stars above, but you can take that with a grain of salt. It is still a great book that will pull you in and not let go. If you are familiar with Grisham’s work, this is where it all began, and I think some consider it mainly downhill from here. Not necessarily a big downhill – but it sure does seem in some aspects like he was at the top of his game for his first few novels. He mentioned in hi</span>
  <span id="freeText9351872825130020295" style="display:none">Original Mid-90s Star Only Review – 5 Stars<br />Re-Read in 2020 Review – 4 Stars<br /><br />You will notice a drop in the stars above, but you can take that with a grain of salt. It is still a great book that will pull you in and not let go. If you are familiar with Grisham’s work, this is where it all began, and I think some consider it mainly downhill from here. Not necessarily a big downhill – but it sure does seem in some aspects like he was at the top of his game for his first few novels. He mentioned in his forward that this one almost did not get published, but the success of The Firm helped generate interest, and I am very glad it did.<br /><br />This is not an easy book to read, but fiction based on hard truths never is. There is very graphic and shocking sexual assault and racism. So, while they add to a powerful story, some may find it difficult to read. Knowing this, be sure to proceed with caution!<br /><br />The reason for the slight downturn in stars for me is that it just didn’t feel as smooth to me as I remembered. Maybe I was looking at an old favorite through rose-colored glassed before I re-read. The thought that kept going through my head, especially after reading the forward and seeing that it almost didn’t get published, is that it felt like it was a bit rough with a lot of coincidences, drawn out scenes followed by rushed scenes, etc. Nothing that was severe enough t ruin the experience, but enough that it was noticeable to me.<br /><br />If you are a Grisham fan, it is likely that you already read this. If you are a Grisham fan and you haven’t read this, I am actually not really sure you can call yourself a Grisham fan! So, you should remedy that right away!</span>

<div id="review_1438704181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1438704181" />
    <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor"><img alt="Fabian {Councillor}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599133151p2/40792319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1438704181?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian {Councillor}" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor">Fabian {Councillor}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=john-grisham">john-grisham</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=legal-drama">legal-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=year-1989">year-1989</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438704181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer987184925624843346">"A Time to Kill" is a riveting story of retribution and justice ... so does the title imply. Replace <i>riveting</i> by <i>frustrating</i> and you know what I felt while reading this doorstopper of a book.<br/><br/>On more than 500 pages, John Grisham delves deep into the schemes and entanglements of a trial in the Southern USA. The premise was so interesting that it was impossible not to pick this book up: A ten-year-old girl is raped by two drunken men, and her father takes the law into his own hands by killing the r</span>
  <span id="freeText987184925624843346" style="display:none">"A Time to Kill" is a riveting story of retribution and justice ... so does the title imply. Replace <i>riveting</i> by <i>frustrating</i> and you know what I felt while reading this doorstopper of a book.<br /><br />On more than 500 pages, John Grisham delves deep into the schemes and entanglements of a trial in the Southern USA. The premise was so interesting that it was impossible not to pick this book up: A ten-year-old girl is raped by two drunken men, and her father takes the law into his own hands by killing the rapists of his daughter. The major problem in this case: The girl and her father are black, and the two rapists are white. If there is one thing Grisham manages to implement perfectly in his story, then it is the exploration of arguments about why the father should be sentenced to death or declared innocent as a result of the circumstances. The reader always bears in his mind how the jury would be reacting in case the roles were reversed - if two black men had raped a white girl of ten years -, but the fact that acquitting the father of his crime would encourage many other people to commit self-administered justice too also needs to be taken into account.<br /><br />Might this premise deliver storytelling material for so many pages? Yes, it might. Only ... it didn't. Shortly after <s>Gary Su</s> Jake Brigance assumed his duty of defending his client, the novel drifted away into long-winded, boring and insignificant rambling. Many people claim this story to be very realistic for how the situation for black people in Mississippi during the 1980's was like. I have never lived there, so I have no idea how real it really was, but the way Jake Brigance acted and behaved definitely did not feel realistic to me. Because who doesn't get royally dunk three days before an important trial? Never before have I been that frustrated by a protagonist who behaved like an asshole towards his wife and just about everyone else he encountered, but was still portrayed like the absolute hero. Throw an incapable prosecutor into the game to make Brigance's light shine even brighter, and you have the perfect Grisham version of Fleming's James Bond.<br /><br />And let's not even address the lack of emotions during the entire novel. You might think that a ten-year-old girl being raped by two drunken men will leave you feeling sorry for her and her family, on the edge of shedding tears? I have to disappoint you, because Grisham's writing deprives every single emotion from every potentially touching scene. You never know how a character feels inside his soul, because Grisham only tells, only allows his reader to guess what his characters might feel at this very moment. <br /><br />1.5 stars, rounded <s>up due to the interesting premise and the very relevant topic</s> down due to me reconsidering the relevance of the rating system Goodreads suggests (1 star equaling "didn't like it").<br /><br />Also, just to clarify things a bit: I didn't dislike the story; the plot was extremely interesting to me and had so much potential, must of which was explored vividly in a very tight and well-structured novel. I also really liked the film adaptation; it may not be a masterpiece, but it's a very well-adapted movie. My main source of frustration is the writing, so in the end I guess I just can't get into John Grisham's writing style, even though I would appreciate the contents of his novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="987184925624843346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=whatever">whatever</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer825996759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6002540620881149430">2.5 stars. One of my least favorites of Grisham's books, and that's saying something. Actually I kind of liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32499.The_Pelican_Brief' title='The Pelican Brief by John Grisham' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Pelican Brief</a> and one or two of his others, but mostly they strike me as mediocre writing combined, more often than not, with pulpit-pounding and breast-beating about some particular legal issue. <br/><br/>In this case the setting is a murder trial for a African-American man who gunned down his 10 year old daughter's rapists, who are stereotypical Southern white trash racists who tried to mur</span>
  <span id="freeText6002540620881149430" style="display:none">2.5 stars. One of my least favorites of Grisham's books, and that's saying something. Actually I kind of liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32499.The_Pelican_Brief" title="The Pelican Brief by John Grisham" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pelican Brief</a> and one or two of his others, but mostly they strike me as mediocre writing combined, more often than not, with pulpit-pounding and breast-beating about some particular legal issue. <br /><br />In this case the setting is a murder trial for a African-American man who gunned down his 10 year old daughter's rapists, who are stereotypical Southern white trash racists who tried to murder this little girl and left her for dead. The legal question is whether jury nullification is sometimes justified, since the father's defense lawyer, Jake Brigance - having no other legal options - is trying to convince the jury to find the father not guilty by reason of temporary insanity. Grisham, as par for the course, loads the dice on that issue. (Biggest clue: the KKK getting involved.)<br /><br />I've only read as many of Grisham's books as I have because my father-in-law (another voracious reader) thought that because I was a lawyer I would automatically like Grisham's books, so I regularly received them from him as birthday and Christmas presents. I never had the heart to tell him I'd prefer another author. My FIL is gone now, may he rest in peace, so no more Grisham for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6002540620881149430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3327593773" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3327593773" />
    <a title="Karina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62428250-karina"><img alt="Karina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541395389p2/62428250.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer18042909178134794050">This is my first John Grisham book, I am embarrassed to admit. I felt like I was in Clanton, Mississippi reliving this gruesome murder. His writing and knowledge on the law system is pretty amazing to read. Makes you realize all the politics and behind the door negotiations going on. <br/><br/>This is a story of two pothead white trash drug dealers that rape a 10-year-old black girl. They urinate on her, tie her legs and hands to a fence and tree, beat her, pour beer on her while she is calling for her da</span>
  <span id="freeText18042909178134794050" style="display:none">This is my first John Grisham book, I am embarrassed to admit. I felt like I was in Clanton, Mississippi reliving this gruesome murder. His writing and knowledge on the law system is pretty amazing to read. Makes you realize all the politics and behind the door negotiations going on. <br /><br />This is a story of two pothead white trash drug dealers that rape a 10-year-old black girl. They urinate on her, tie her legs and hands to a fence and tree, beat her, pour beer on her while she is calling for her daddy to save her. This is not a spoiler.<br /><br />Now what happens when black daddy is pissed at the system and takes these two white guys into his own hands? Will the color of his skin get him convicted in KKK town or will the jury understand that he was a loving angry father? (I personally rooted for Carl Lee. Sometimes our system just fails us and we want to be the vigilante except Carl Lee actually had the balls to do it)<br /><br />"At eleven-fifteen it rang again, and Jake received his first death threat, anonymous of course. He was called a nigger-loving son of a bitch, one who would not live if the nigger walked." (pg. 85)</span>

  <span id="freeText7019477821645389237" style="display:none">This was John Grisham' s very first book.He dreamed of getting it published,and went through innumerable rejections.It was largely ignored,when it was first published.Grisham was inspired by an actual court room case to write it.<br /><br />It is about rape,retribution and racial violence,in the American South.A young black girl is raped,and her outraged father takes justice into his own hands.A young defence attorney tries to save his life,only to find himself in danger.And then comes all that racial violence,which resembles what has been happening recently in the US.<br /><br />It is a first book,and it rambles.<br />At over 500 pages,it is too lengthy.This story could have been told so much better in half the number of pages,or even less.</span>

<div id="review_95403407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95403407" />
    <a title="James Thane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane"><img alt="James Thane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442513566p2/3483907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95403407?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Thane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Thane" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane">James Thane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=legal-thrillers">legal-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95403407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer185870840006824720">I confess that when one of my book clubs made this our monthly selection, I approached it with more than a little trepidation. I knew that this was Grisham's first book and that when it was first published as a hardcover, he could hardly give it away. Sales were so poor that there was initially no paperback release. Only after the success of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5358.The_Firm' title='The Firm by John Grisham' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Firm</a> and other of Grisham's books was this one finally resurrected and released in paperback.<br/><br/>Like most of Grisham's other readers, I jumped aboard the t</span>
  <span id="freeText185870840006824720" style="display:none">I confess that when one of my book clubs made this our monthly selection, I approached it with more than a little trepidation. I knew that this was Grisham's first book and that when it was first published as a hardcover, he could hardly give it away. Sales were so poor that there was initially no paperback release. Only after the success of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5358.The_Firm" title="The Firm by John Grisham" rel="nofollow noopener">The Firm</a> and other of Grisham's books was this one finally resurrected and released in paperback.<br /><br />Like most of Grisham's other readers, I jumped aboard the train with <i>The Firm</i> and never looked back. Though I've enjoyed most of his later books, I simply took it for granted that this first effort was probably his "practice" novel, that it was not very good, and hence the poor sales. I further assumed that his publisher, anxious to milk the Grisham brand for all it was worth, only finally published <i>A Time to Kill</i> in paper simply to cash in. Accordingly, I've avoided it all these years until I was finally forced to read it.<br /><br />I'm very happy that I was. The book turned out to be a gripping story with better-defined characters and a much more interesting setting than many of Grisham's later books. In fact, it may be one of his best.<br /><br />The tiny town of Clanton, Mississippi, is shocked when two drunk and drug-addled thugs viciously assault a ten-year-old girl, failing to kill her only because they could not find a bridge from which to throw the child. The two are quickly arrested and charged with various crimes related to the attack, when the girl's father, a decorated Vietnam vet, takes the law into his own hands and kills the men who so gruesomely violated his daughter.<br /><br />The father hires a young, up-and-coming lawyer named Jake Brigance to represent him. But this is Mississippi and the case is complicated by the fact that the victim and her father are black while the two dead thugs were white. The population of the town is evenly divided between blacks and whites and, while most people irrespective of race, condemn the actions of the two thugs, they are divided, mostly along racial lines, over the issue of whether the father should be convicted of premeditated murder or be given a medal for ridding the town of the two scumbags.<br /><br />Grisham plays fair with both sides, and it's clear that he knows very well the setting, the people and the dynamics of the situation. There are a number of great characters in this novel and very few of them are pure of heart. These are much more complex characters than those usually served up in books like this, and the story grabs you from the start. It also raises a lot of thought-provoking questions. It's a great read, and I'm only sorry that it took me so long to get to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="185870840006824720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3563382145" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3563382145" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57725883-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557030750p2/57725883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3563382145?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/57725883-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio Cassette 9780553700671" href="/book/show/1514486.A_Time_to_Kill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57725883-rob?shelf=courtroom-thriller">courtroom-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57725883-rob?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3563382145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1224190731353818167">A courtroom thriller published 1989<br/><br/>This is John Grisham’s first novel but not his first published.<br/>The setting is in Mississippi where, even in 1989, the divide between the white and the black communities was still very obvious. And guess what, here we are 41 years later and what’s changed, not much it would seem.<br/><br/>A little ten year old black girl is brutally raped and beaten. She is found and taken to the hospital where the doctors put her back together physically but her emotional condition is no</span>
  <span id="freeText1224190731353818167" style="display:none">A courtroom thriller published 1989<br /><br />This is John Grisham’s first novel but not his first published.<br />The setting is in Mississippi where, even in 1989, the divide between the white and the black communities was still very obvious. And guess what, here we are 41 years later and what’s changed, not much it would seem.<br /><br />A little ten year old black girl is brutally raped and beaten. She is found and taken to the hospital where the doctors put her back together physically but her emotional condition is not so easily fixed. When the doctors tell the family that she will heal but she will never be able to have children of her own her daddy swears he will make the monsters that did this pay and pay dearly.<br /><br />Two men, both white, are soon caught and charged with the crime. But this is a predominantly white town and the chances that they will get what they deserve is remote.<br /><br />To make sure that justice is truly served Carl Lee, the father, decides to take the law into his own hands and shoot the accused men. This he does and by the time he was finished they were both well and truly dead.<br /><br />Carl Lee is of course charged with murder on two accounts.<br /><br />Enter Jack Brigance, a young white lawyer and the man charged with getting Carl Lee acquitted of the charge of murder.<br /><br />What follows is courtroom thriller with racially fuelled violence from both sides of the racial divide. <br /><br />I enjoyed this book although I found it to be overly long and suffered from a bit too much irrelevant information. But over all an entertaining read.<br /><br />A 4 stars recommendation<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1994587947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1994587947" />
    <a title="Andre Gonzalez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53583787-andre-gonzalez"><img alt="Andre Gonzalez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546573233p2/53583787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1994587947?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andre Gonzalez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andre Gonzalez" href="/user/show/53583787-andre-gonzalez">Andre Gonzalez</a>
      </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1994587947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1889560476711906515">This book totally rocked my world! I had asked for a legal thriller as a recommendation and I'm glad to have this one suggested! The racial tension in this story felt as real as it did in To Kill A Mockingbird. I felt I was right there in Clanton, Mississippi trying to dodge the KKK and marching with everyone else. This is my first Grisham novel, and I'll definitely be exploring more!</span>

Hats off to him! A truly heroic lawyer in the image of Atticus Finch.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1647059451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1647059451" />
    <a title="Shaun" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9779623-shaun"><img alt="Shaun" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565572877p2/9779623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1647059451?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaun" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaun" href="/user/show/9779623-shaun">Shaun</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780922066032" href="/book/show/1177118.A_Time_to_Kill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9779623-shaun?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1647059451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5306125286817045033">A satisfying legal thriller.<br/><br/>Grisham gives the reader much to ponder in this story of a black man who kills two men who raped and brutally beat his 10 year-old daughter. It's hard not to root for the father. It also makes one wonder if the story would have worked as well had it been his wife or sister who had been raped instead (probably not), which in and of itself is worth thinking about. It certainly makes one wonder if and when murder is ever justifiable, and exactly how we draw those lines i</span>
  <span id="freeText5306125286817045033" style="display:none">A satisfying legal thriller.<br /><br />Grisham gives the reader much to ponder in this story of a black man who kills two men who raped and brutally beat his 10 year-old daughter. It's hard not to root for the father. It also makes one wonder if the story would have worked as well had it been his wife or sister who had been raped instead (probably not), which in and of itself is worth thinking about. It certainly makes one wonder if and when murder is ever justifiable, and exactly how we draw those lines in the sand as individuals and as a society.<br /><br />That said, there were times the characters felt one dimensional. Lots of stereotypes. Occasionally, the story and the characters bordered on satire. Toward the end I grew weary of the tongue-and-cheek dialogue between characters. I also felt Grisham offers a very cynical view of lawyers and the legal process, which at times adds to the story and at other times takes away from it.<br /><br />Overall, an incredibly well-written story, with relevant and important themes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5306125286817045033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6783309686577054993">Continuing with my reading of all Grisham titles. This is the first I've read of the southern trial novels. Extensive use of the N word was disturbing but it's used for an accurate portrayal of the voice of white southerners of the period, not gratuitously. Much more disturbing was the scene of the violent attack on a little girl that's the basis of the story. Again, not gratuitous. This novel was based on a true story. A thoughtful and thought provoking reminder of the cruelty and racial prejud</span>
  <span id="freeText6783309686577054993" style="display:none">Continuing with my reading of all Grisham titles. This is the first I've read of the southern trial novels. Extensive use of the N word was disturbing but it's used for an accurate portrayal of the voice of white southerners of the period, not gratuitously. Much more disturbing was the scene of the violent attack on a little girl that's the basis of the story. Again, not gratuitous. This novel was based on a true story. A thoughtful and thought provoking reminder of the cruelty and racial prejudice in our not-so-far past. Really interesting descriptions of the trial and the jury and its deliberations.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/17448500-a-time-to-kill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6658001-terence-m-spring-is-in-my-step?shelf=listened-read-twice">listened-read-twice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6658001-terence-m-spring-is-in-my-step?shelf=read-then-listened">read-then-listened</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223142044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8296671144446100062">Audiobook - 12:21 hours - Narrator: Robert Petkoff<br/><b>3.0 out of 5.0 stars - "I Liked It"</b> (Second "reading")<br/><br/>My GR friend Tim read this a few weeks ago and awarded it a very rare, for him, 10 out of 10 stars. Because of this, I decided to <s>read</s> listen to it for a second time.<br/><br/>I first read "A Time to Kill" as a paperback in the early 1990's, following John Grisham's huge success with "The Firm", "The Pelican Brief", and those that followed annually in his first decade as a top-line author. As I tuned in</span>
  <span id="freeText8296671144446100062" style="display:none">Audiobook - 12:21 hours - Narrator: Robert Petkoff<br /><b>3.0 out of 5.0 stars - "I Liked It"</b> (Second "reading")<br /><br />My GR friend Tim read this a few weeks ago and awarded it a very rare, for him, 10 out of 10 stars. Because of this, I decided to <s>read</s> listen to it for a second time.<br /><br />I first read "A Time to Kill" as a paperback in the early 1990's, following John Grisham's huge success with "The Firm", "The Pelican Brief", and those that followed annually in his first decade as a top-line author. As I tuned into this audiobook, I realised how little I remembered about Jack Brigance and the rather motley crew he surrounded himself with in Mississippi as he mounted a defence for black Carl-Lee Harley's killing of two white men who had raped, beaten and left his ten-years old daughter to die.<br /><br />I am not surprised that I "liked" (3-stars) rather than "really liked" (4-stars) "A Time to Kill" because there wasn't much to "really like". Jack Brigance was hardly a likeable character and there was plenty not to like about his treatment of some of the women in the story. His dismissive attitude towards his wife, his downright rudeness towards his secretary and his holier-than-thou attitude towards "Ro-Ark" (sp?), the highly unlikely and (literally) unbelievably skilled and precocious clerk who worked for him for free, producing 'outstanding' briefs and other paperwork in (metaphorically) no time at all. The fate of this "Northerner" and also of the various KKK members and the local Klavern were left dangling as Grisham seemed in a rush to finish this already wordy and over-long novel.<br /><br />My GR friend Tim and I seem to have similar attitudes towards John Grisham novels. We either "loved this one", "liked that one", "couldn't finish the other one", but not always referring to the same novels. <br /><br />I have 34 novels in my Grisham collection (including "The Reckoning" released this month) and 10 are unread or unheard. Of the 24 read or listened to, 16 are rated three stars or more and eight are rated one star or dnf. So, at the moment I enjoy two out of every three Grisham novels and that is a pretty good average. Note: not all my novels are listed in my Goodreads profile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8296671144446100062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2406442319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17745904357167719094">5 Stars. Not as great as "To Kill a Mockingbird" when it comes to race relations and the law in the southern US, but both deserve a hearty 5. Maybe "Mockingbird" a 5.3? One difference is the point of view; a young girl, now a woman, is the narrator of the story set in the mid 1930s. It's endearing and full of love for her father, Atticus. "Time to Kill" is novel of our times, the 2020s. Although it focuses on the 1980s, it's a courtroom drama which reels from a string of brutal events. The resol</span>
  <span id="freeText17745904357167719094" style="display:none">5 Stars. Not as great as "To Kill a Mockingbird" when it comes to race relations and the law in the southern US, but both deserve a hearty 5. Maybe "Mockingbird" a 5.3? One difference is the point of view; a young girl, now a woman, is the narrator of the story set in the mid 1930s. It's endearing and full of love for her father, Atticus. "Time to Kill" is novel of our times, the 2020s. Although it focuses on the 1980s, it's a courtroom drama which reels from a string of brutal events. The resolution is less nuanced. Both expose attitudes prevalent in the white community - ignorance, condescension, and among many, hatred. Yet if you look carefully, a touch of progress, no more than that, can be found. The argument which wins the day in the trial of black Carl-Lee Hailey likely could not have been made fifty years earlier. He murdered two despicable white supremacists who raped and beat his 10-year-old daughter Tonya. They bragged about it! "Time" is replete with KKK burning crosses and a tolerance for racism by some that will make you cringe. Lawyer Jake Brigance does his best but it's uphill all the way! For once the movie version is just as good. (September 2020)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17745904357167719094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_892367323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/892367323" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/892367323?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer892367323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7135819011021218054">Before returning to Clanton Mississippi and Ford County, I took some time to refresh myself of my first journey here, to see where the Grisham journey had its humble roots. While it is likely this novel is not the traditional 'must-read' before diving into SYCAMORE ROW, I chose to remember the powerful novel that Grisham admits barely made a blip on the radar until after THE FIRM pushed him to the top of all the reading lists. This is a wonderful book that introduces readers to a Mississippi whe</span>
  <span id="freeText7135819011021218054" style="display:none">Before returning to Clanton Mississippi and Ford County, I took some time to refresh myself of my first journey here, to see where the Grisham journey had its humble roots. While it is likely this novel is not the traditional 'must-read' before diving into SYCAMORE ROW, I chose to remember the powerful novel that Grisham admits barely made a blip on the radar until after THE FIRM pushed him to the top of all the reading lists. This is a wonderful book that introduces readers to a Mississippi where desegregation is no more than a word in the dictionary. When the brutal rape of a 10 year old black girl makes small ripples amongst the vast majority of Ford County's white population, the townsfolk continue with life as usual, leaving the black population to mourn the injustice. All, that is, but Carl-Lee Haley, father of the victim. The two white men accused of the rape are charged and the legal process begins its slow march. When Haley takes things into his own hands and shoots both men while they are in the courthouse, the ripples turn to tidal waves, dividing the town along racial lines. After Jake Brigance, town lawyer and admitted liberal, agrees to take the case, all eyes are on him and how he will argue a case that appears cut and dry. Using an insanity angle, Brigance tries to sway popular opinion in a county where black rights are all but nil. This small county soon has the eyes of the entire country as support on both sides heightens. It is only when the Klan begin enacting their own form of justice that violence and retribution stain the Mississippi legal process. Brigance begins building a defence, using the meagre $900 offered to him while his family chooses to protect themselves when he refuses to follow. Using an odd patchwork legal team whose interest in the case outweighs their desire for payment, Brigance brings the case forward. Before a jury of his peers, Haley is presented as a grieving father and man whose mind was completely altered by the acts of two drug addicts. As the city is torn apart, Brigance can only hope that justice is truly colour-blind in the racist south. Grisham planted the seed of legal literary excellence with this novel and it should be required reading for the legal thriller fanatic.<br /><br />Grisham does so much in this novel on so many levels. From addressing the ne'er-spoken race divide in the South as it relates to legal equity to the nuances of courtroom thrillers for which he will become famous, to the formulaic storyline of the lawyer swimming against the tide on the side of justice all issues come out front and centre throughout the novel. Grisham tackles all these as a complete unknown in the literary field and does not stray away from strong social commentary throughout. While I will admit my mind flashed to the wonderfully done film based on the novel throughout the reading, I could see and feel the characters develop on the page and take life. Without throwing punches, Grisham dispels the rumours that desegregation stopped the race riots and that all is well throughout the country. Speaking about what he knows best--the law and Mississippi--Grisham brings the reader into the fold and captures them with riveting narration, stellar legal description, and a set of characters whose perfection within the story has them fit like the proverbial glove. This was surely the novel that got the Grisham craze started and, to me, proves to be one of his timeless classics.<br /><br />As an added aside, I cannot leave this review without presenting what may seem like quite the far-fetched claim. As I listened to the audiobook version of this novel, I could not help but wonder if Grisham sought to create a newer version of the Harpee Lee classic, To Kill a Mockingbird, bringing the injustice of the law between the races to the forefront. While Brigance is no Atticus Finch, this parallel cannot be disregarded as the reader sees the tension building and the complete despair of the defence counsel as the evidence pours forward. While I am almost certain Grisham would deny its connection, the reader who has taken the time to read both will surely see some similarities in both. Have things changed much since 1960? Since 1989? Surely some steps have been made in this regard, but I would venture to say that the two novels, which act as strong social commentaries, are not far off from what is still going on.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Grisham, for allowing me such a raw glimpse into the realm of justice in the South and not candy coating it in the least. Onward to SYCAMORE ROW... with a plethora of characters in my quiver and a passion for Ford County once again!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7135819011021218054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3582754569332385662" style="display:none">There are 104 pages of review on this book, and I read two pages worth and agreed with a dozen or so. I always wondered why cheap thrillers like this book never get discussed in great literature classes and I think I can answer that question. 1. Because there is no interpretation. Books like this are no brainers. Little thinking is required.<br />That's really it. <br />Now for the book review. First of all, Grisham needed like 1 or 2 more pages to close out. He rushed the ending. <br />Sure it was a great thriller. It posed a great ethical question- Is it ever right to take the justice system in your own hand? This was a thriller, so I gave it a 3. <br /><br />I don't know. The whole book left me feeling really empty and thinking what am I doing wasting my time reading these types of books? </span>

<div id="review_1966132002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1966132002" />
    <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf"><img alt="Cody | CodysBookshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592500568p2/56352820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1966132002?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody | CodysBookshelf" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf">Cody | CodysBookshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385470810" href="/book/show/1038927.A_Time_to_Kill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=john-grisham">john-grisham</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1966132002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3372627908899036854">My first John Grisham novel was his latest release, <i>The Whistler</i>: a capable, if not entirely thrilling, read. Because I give every author two chances to 'wow' me, I decided to take a stab at Grisham's debut, <i>A Time to Kill</i>. <br/><br/>Wow. Wow wow wow. Was I impressed! <br/><br/>Set in northeastern Mississippi (an area I've ridden through many times, and have a certain affection for), a young black girl is kidnapped and brutally raped by two white rednecks, both career criminals despite only being in their twenties.</span>
  <span id="freeText3372627908899036854" style="display:none">My first John Grisham novel was his latest release, <i>The Whistler</i>: a capable, if not entirely thrilling, read. Because I give every author two chances to 'wow' me, I decided to take a stab at Grisham's debut, <i>A Time to Kill</i>. <br /><br />Wow. Wow wow wow. Was I impressed! <br /><br />Set in northeastern Mississippi (an area I've ridden through many times, and have a certain affection for), a young black girl is kidnapped and brutally raped by two white rednecks, both career criminals despite only being in their twenties. The two are caught and arrested, but that does not make the girl's pain go away, of course — so her father takes matters into his own hands, and murders the two rapists in cold blood. Jake Brigance, a young lawyer who is desperate for the big time, takes the case despite its daunting nature. What unravels is something that thoroughly impacts the entire fictional town of Clanton, Mississippi, and the reader as well. There is no black or white here, only a world of gray; while most readers can sympathize with the girl's father, was it right of him to murder the men? What is morally justifiable? What role does the court system play in our lives, and even when juries make the 'right' decision, is it still wrong? These are questions Grisham leads the reader to, never fully answering them but instead inspiring thought and meditation. I know I certainly look at the American justice system in a new light after reading this fabulous novel. <br /><br />This was a journey that had me glued to the pages, and I would have read it much faster had life not intervened. I was shocked by how fleshed out the town of Clanton and its inhabitants really are, in the pages of this weighty story; Grisham is one who can tell a tale, and had that talent from the very beginning . . . as is evident here, in his debut novel. I was not sure what I wanted the final decision to be — guilty, not guilty, mistrial — because of all the twists and turns and new revelations that come to light during this volume's 480-ish pages. That's a good thing. The person who begins reading this novel and the person who finishes this novel aren't the same, not completely; this is one with true potential to impact, all these years later. It really stands up. <br /><br />John Grisham is one of America's most popular authors, and I can now see why. I cannot wait to work my way through the rest of his releases, but I don't know if any of them can top this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3372627908899036854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1442981938" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442981938" />
    <a title="Piyangie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie"><img alt="Piyangie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590579939p2/48056505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1442981938?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piyangie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piyangie" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie">Piyangie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099537038" href="/book/show/10227879-a-time-to-kill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=legal-thrillers">legal-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=favorite-contemporary">favorite-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1442981938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3296456662867087287">Reading Sycamore Row took me down the memory lane to its prequel, A Time to Kill. And I realized that I haven't written a review for this much beloved book. So here I'm trying to rectify that omission. <br/><br/><i> A Time to Kill </i> is one of the few emotional contemporary books that I have read. Based on the theme of racism and set in mid-eighties in a southern town in Mississippi, Grisham tells the tale of a black man who murdered two white men who raped his child and one white lawyer's heroic struggle to d</span>
  <span id="freeText3296456662867087287" style="display:none">Reading Sycamore Row took me down the memory lane to its prequel, A Time to Kill. And I realized that I haven't written a review for this much beloved book. So here I'm trying to rectify that omission. <br /><br /><i> A Time to Kill </i> is one of the few emotional contemporary books that I have read. Based on the theme of racism and set in mid-eighties in a southern town in Mississippi, Grisham tells the tale of a black man who murdered two white men who raped his child and one white lawyer's heroic struggle to defend him in a racially prejudiced society amidst great personal losses. <br /><br />Jake Brigance, the young hero, is undoubtedly my favourite Grisham character; and it will forever be so. Being a lawyer myself, he represents many ethical and professional qualities that we lawyers revere. Perhaps, he was modeled on the author himself. <br /><br />In the story, Jake represents the future, the liberal promising mind of a racially prejudiced southern town. His struggle to make the jury look beyond the colour of the man and into the heart of the man to understand (not to condone) his action, is a fight for equality and justice in the eyes of law irrespective of a person’s skin colour. And the all-white jury decision is a victory of humanity; a promise that humanity is preserved in average citizens no matter how much division the extremists may create. <br /><br />Although this story is set in a bygone era, it is still relevant for today, for prejudices based on skin colour, gender and religion are still in store. So in that light, <i> A Time to Kill </i> is a timeless tale. <br /><br />And before I end my short review I must say a few words about Grisham's writing. It is his first attempt at a novel, so perhaps the writing is not yet at his best. But it is written with sincerity, compassion and with much feeling that I personally feel that this is the one novel (although his debut) in to which the author has poured his heart and soul. I've read quite a few Grisham work, and to me, <i> A Time to Kill </i> is his best; and it will always be my favourite Grisham novel.<br />.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3296456662867087287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1787660802" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1787660802" />
    <a title="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower"><img alt="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467816536p2/29402776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1787660802?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" href="/user/show/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower">The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/1054051.Die_Jury">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=crime-thriller">crime-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787660802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12158066880079916554"><b>4 stars!</b><br/><br/><i>Die Jury</i> - A Time To Kill in English – was the first Grisham I have read. I’ve heard about him and his books a lot, but somehow I kept going back for other authors I already knew. But I have to say that I enjoyed this one a lot. <br/><br/>I won’t write anything about the plot itself – most people know it anyways, either because there are tons of good summarizing reviews out there, or because they have read or seen the movie (which isn’t nearly as good as the book) themselves. So let me just say a </span>
  <span id="freeText12158066880079916554" style="display:none"><b>4 stars!</b><br /><br /><i>Die Jury</i> - A Time To Kill in English – was the first Grisham I have read. I’ve heard about him and his books a lot, but somehow I kept going back for other authors I already knew. But I have to say that I enjoyed this one a lot. <br /><br />I won’t write anything about the plot itself – most people know it anyways, either because there are tons of good summarizing reviews out there, or because they have read or seen the movie (which isn’t nearly as good as the book) themselves. So let me just say a little about what I liked: <br /><br /><b>American law</b> is always something a little mysterious and – let’s just say it – a little crazy for me. It is very different from what we know in Europe and I was super curious to get a little information on the American system in this book and I have to say that <b>the parts of the book set in the courthouse were by far the ones I enjoyed the most</b>. It was very interesting to see how the process developed and what possibilities the different parties had to act and react. The <b>selection of the jury and its discussions afterwards</b> was very well done. <br /><br />It took a little to really get into the book – the first scene was of course heartbreaking and totally catchy, but the <b>introduction of so many characters in such a short time</b> made my head spin. I still kept mixing up some of them during the book. I really liked our main character <b>Jake Brigance</b>, he might not be the usual super hero and has some <b>serious character issues</b>, but that made him very <b>credible</b>. <br /><br />I also had a few problems with the <b>pace of the plot</b>. I had the feeling that we had a <b>furious start</b>, followed by a <b>very slow middle part</b> which ended in a <b>too fast ending</b>. I guess that such things come with experience and we have to keep in mind that this is <b>Grisham’s first novel</b>. <br /><br />Well, I will definitely keep my eyes out for other Grisham books! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12158066880079916554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IBqnTkFySYhfs7IrBfz8XIcPfwpYJVOT3Ko5gA+DgbAaPM6c+iyA4PiYBkryCfaDUVCYwpao3fSH1H8xwsBzKg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OwaPufpQDG0sbzVTYph++8+32K6xuhAWBXF7xmGrmGEBIOZrQQ7FBYtEgTKVbXQkGeg/Zn83nnFeDz13rOhq+w==')})
  }

Eventually Jill joins the Murder Club, and the four ladies share private interdepartmental information in an effort to track and stop the killer before he strikes again.\n\nThe major subplot -- Lindsay\'s facing up to her illness even while she learns to fall in love again -- carefully compensates for the novel\'s coarse scenes of brutality. Lindsay Boxer is\'t merely an obsessed cop trailing a maniac; she\'s also a terrified woman confronting the onslaught of disease. The story lines balance out to show us the true mettle of someone who puts the safety of others before her own.\n\nAgain, Patterson\'s skill for producing furiously paced fiction are evident as the novel breezes by rapidly.
